1. A 2-year-old child on examination presents with hepatosplenomegaly, cataract, and delayed mental development. Blood galactose levels are high. What hereditary pathology is likely in this child?
a. Galactosemia
b. Hypovitaminosis D
c. Phenylketonuria
d. Disaccharide intolerance
e. Porphyria

2. A man presents with disturbed circulation in the myocardium of the right atrium. The disturbances occurred in the system of the following artery:
*a. Right coronary artery
b. Anterior interventricular branch of the left coronary artery
c. Left coronary artery
d. Right and left coronary arteries
e. Circumflex branch of the left coronary artery

3. A person entered a room with increased levels of carbon dioxide in the air. How will the breathing of this person change?
*a. Respiration rate and depth will increase
b. Respiration depth will increase
c. Respiration rate will increase
d. Respiration rate will decrease
e. Respiration depth will decrease

4. A man has a vitamin D deficiency, which causes the malabsorption of:
*a. Calcium
b. Sodium
c. Iron
d. Water
e. Chlorine

5. A 38-year-old woman complains of constant thirst, frequent urination, low appetite, and headache. Her urine is colorless, clear, slightly acidic, without glucose. Her 24-hour diuresis is up to 12 liters. This condition can be caused by low levels of a certain hormone. Name this hormone:
a. Insulin
b. Glucagon
*c. Vasopressin
d. Atrial natriuretic factor
e. Noradrenaline

6. The mother's karyotype has 45 chromosomes. It was determined that translocation of chromosome 21 to chromosome 14 had occurred. What disorder is likely to be observed in the child of this woman if the father's karyotype is normal?
a. Edwards syndrome
*b. Down syndrome
c. Klinefelter syndrome
d. Morris syndrome (androgen insensitivity)
e. Patau syndrome

7. Acetylsalicylic acid and glucocorticoids both have a marked anti-inflammatory effect. However, unlike glucocorticoids, acetylsalicylic acid has no effect on the synthesis of:
a. Leukotrienes
b. Prostacyclins
c. Thromboxanes
d. Prostaglandins F
e. Prostaglandins E

8. Examination revealed that the patient has an insufficient immunoglobulin count. The likely cause of this finding is a disfunction of the following immune system cells:
a. T-killers
b. T-suppressors
c. T-helpers
d. Plasmablasts
e. Plasma cells

9. The patient's blood test shows a significant increase in the activity of the MB-fraction of CPK (creatine phosphokinase) and LDH-1. What pathology can it indicate?
a. Rheumatism
b. Cholecystitis
c. Hepatitis
*d. Myocardial infarction
e. Pancreatitis

10. X-ray detected a basilar skull fracture. The fracture line passes through the foramen spinosum and foramen rotundum. What bone was damaged as a result of the injury?
a. Occipital bone
b. Ethmoid bone
c. Temporal bone
d. Frontal bone
*e. Sphenoid bone

11. A 55-year-old man was prescribed an antituberculosis agent as a part of his complex therapy for pulmonary tuberculosis. Which of the listed drugs has antibacterial activity only towards Mycobacterium tuberculosis?
a. Gatifloxacin
b. Kanamycin sulfate
c. Isoniazid
d. Streptomycin sulfate
e. Cycloserine

12. A 6-year-old girl presents with acute onset of a disease. She developed sore throat and high temperature that were later accompanied by a punctate skin rash. Oral examination reveals acute pharyngeal hyperemia, raspberry tongue, and enlarged bright red tonsils with dull gray and yellow foci that spread to the peritonsillar tissues. The submandibular lymph nodes are enlarged. What disease are these changes characteristic of?
a. Pharyngeal diphtheria
*b. Scarlet fever
c. Laryngeal diphtheria
d. Measles
e. Meningococcal nasopharyngitis

13. In a scientific experiment, a structure in one of the cell components has been destroyed, impairing the cell's ability to divide. What structure has been destroyed?
a. Mitochondria
b. Glycocalyx
*c. Centrosome
d. Microfibrils
e. Ribosomes

14. Several months after giving birth, a woman became inert, her teeth and hair started falling out and she started losing weight. Her blood pressure, body temperature, and blood glucose are low. Examination shows low blood levels of growth hormone and adrenocorticotropic hormone. What functional disturbance of pituitary gland is observed in the patient?
a. Cushing disease
b. Acromegalia
c. Diabetes insipidus
*d. Panhypopituitarism
e. Hypophyseal nanism

15. A genetic defect of a Na^+-dependent transporter of monosaccharides of the enterocyte membrane causes the development of malabsorption syndrome in newborn babies as a result of impaired absorption. In this case, impaired absorption of the following substance would be observed:
a. Maltose
*b. Galactose
c. Lactose
d. Sucrose
e. Ribose

16. The breakdown of glycogen in the liver is stimulated by glucagon. What secondary messenger (intermediary) forms in the cell in this case?
a. cGMP
*b. cAMP
c. Diacylglycerol
d. Nitrous oxide
e. Carbon monoxide

17. A 36-year-old man was brought into the infectious diseases hospital with profuse diarrhea, signs of exsiccosis, and acute decrease of body temperature. He died of uremia. Autopsy detects a colorless liquid resembling rice water in the lumen of the small intestine; mucosa is hyperemic. Microscopy of the small intestine shows vascular plethora, focal hemorrhages, desquamation of enterocytes, goblet cell hypersecretion, and lymphocytic and leukocytic infiltration of mucosal stroma. What is the most likely diagnosis?
a. Salmonellosis
b. Dysentery
c. Crohn disease
d. Typhoid fever
*e. Cholera

18. Certain vessels look like blunt-ended, flattened, endothelial tubes and have no basement membrane or pericytes. Their endothelium is affixed with anchoring filaments to the collagen fibers of the connective tissue. Name these vessels.
a. Venules
*b. Lymphatic capillaries
c. Hemocapillaries
d. Arterio-venous anastomoses
e. Arterioles

19. Examination of a boy revealed that he was unable to pucker his lips into a tube. He cannot blow out a candle, the corners of his mouth do not lift during laughing, and his oral fissure stretches to the sides (transverse smile). What muscle is likely to be atrophied in this case, as indicated by these symptoms?
a. Masseter
b. Buccinator
c. Risorius
d. Orbicularis oris
e. Zygomaticus major muscle

20. A patient with chronic tonsillitis has developed a complication - a retropharyngeal abscess. Into what structure can the infection spread from the retropharyngeal (retrovisceral) space?
a. Previsceral space
b. Suprasternal interaponeurotic space
c. Thoracic cavity, posterior mediastinum
d. Thoracic cavity, middle mediastinum
e. Thoracic cavity, anterior mediastinum

21. To determine toxigenicity of diphtheria causative agents obtained from patients, the cultures were inoculated in a Petri dish with nutrient agar, bilaterally to a strip of filter paper spotted with antidiphtheric antitoxic serum and situated in the center of the Petri dish. After incubation of the inoculated cultures in the agar, strip-like areas of medium turbidity formed between some of the cultures and the filter paper. What immunological test was conducted?
a. Opsonization test
b. Agglutination test
c. Coombs test
d. Ring precipitin test
*e. Agar gel precipitation test

22. Histology of an eyeball wall microslide shows a structure consisting of a chain of three neurons. The bodies of these neurons form an outer layer, an inner nuclear layer, and a ganglion layer. What structure of the eye has such a morphology?
a. Vascular membrane
*b. Retina
c. Sclera
d. Iris
e. Ciliary body

23. The height of a 10-year-old child is 178 cm, while the child's weight is 64 kg. What endocrine gland is dysfunctional in the child, causing this condition?
a. Gonads
b. Thyroid gland
c. Adrenal glands
*d. Pituitary gland
e. Parathyroid gland

24. The causative agent of tuberculosis can exist both intracellularly and extracellularly, as well as in caseous necrosis. What drug can have a harmful effect on Mycobacterium tuberculosis of any localization?
a. Isoniazid
*b. Rifampicin
c. Streptomycin
d. Sodium aminosalicylate
e. Ethambutol

25. A 35-year-old woman came for a follow-up visit two weeks after a case of COVID-19. ECG detects a decrease in the voltage of the waves, the P wave is unchanged and connected to the QRS complex, the duration of the PQ interval is 0.32 seconds. What type of arrhythmia did the patient develop?
a. Sinoatrial block
b. Third-degree atrioventricular block
c. Second-degree atrioventricular block
d. First-degree atrioventricular block
e. Wolff-Parkinson-White syndrome

26. A patient developed a painful red nodule in the area of the lower jaw. Histologically, accumulation of purulent exudate was detected in several hair follicles. What clinical and morphological type of inflammation is observed in this case?
a. Felon (panaritium)
b. Furuncle
c. Abscess
*d. Carbuncle
e. Phlegmon

27. After a maxillofacial injury, a 40-year-old man developed a disfunction of the sublingual and submandibular glands on the left. Hyposalivation is observed in the affected glands. What nerve does not function properly in this case?
a. Cranial nerve X
b. Cranial nerve VI
c. Cranial nerve XII
*d. Cranial nerve VII
e. Cranial nerve XI

28. A patient has been diagnosed with peptic ulcer disease of the stomach and hyperacidity. Endoscopical and bacteriological testing allowed isolating Helicobacter bacteria. What characteristic of these microorganisms allows them to survive in the acidic environment of the stomach?
a. Oxidase activity
b. Catalase activity
c. Resistance to vancomycin
d. Capsule formation
*e. Urease activity

29. Dystrophic changes in the cardiac muscle are accompanied by dilation of the heart chambers, decreased force of cardiac contractions, increased volume of the blood that remains in the heart chambers during systole, and venous overflow. What medical condition can be characterized by these phenomena?
a. Myogenic dilatation
b. Stage of cardiosclerosis
c. Tonogenic dilatation
d. Developing stage of myocardial hypertrophy
e. Cardiac tamponade

30. A 25-year-old man came to a neurologist with complaints of a weakness in his legs and disturbed gait. The doctor diagnosed him with myasthenia gravis and prescribed him proserin injections. What is the mechanism of action of this medicine?
*a. Anticholinesterase action
b. Direct-acting cholinomimetic
c. Metabolic stimulant
d. Inhibitor of braking processes
e. Acetylcholine synthesis activator

31. To suppress autoimmune response after organ transplantation, a course of hormone therapy is mandatory. What hormones are used for this purpose?
a. Sex hormones
b. Adrenaline
c. Somatotropin
*d. Glucocorticoids
e. Mineralocorticoids

32. Autopsy of a 60-year-old woman, who for a long time had been suffering from essential hypertension, shows significantly diminished kidneys (weight of both kidneys is 80 g) with finely granular surface. Uniform renal cortical thinning can be observed on section. Name the described changes in the kidneys:
a. Amyloid contracted kidney
b. Secondary contracted kidney
c. Pyelonephritic contracted kidney
*d. Primary contracted kidney
e. Diabetic nephrosclerosis

33. A 45-year-old patient came to a doctor with complaints of headache, dizziness, frequent nausea, vomiting, muscle weakness, and pain in the area of the heart. Blood pressure  - 170/110 mm Hg. Sodium levels in peripheral blood  - 165 mmol/L, potassium levels  - 2.5 mmol/L. Computed tomography detected a tumor 1 cm in size in the left adrenal gland. What changes in the acid-base balance would be observed in this case?
a. Respiratory alkalosis
b. Respiratory acidosis
c. Metabolic acidosis
d. No acid-base imbalance occurs
*e. Metabolic alkalosis
